<div id="review_1289257122" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1289257122" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1289257122?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19126246-kaitlin?shelf=my-sff-faves">my-sff-faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1289257122" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3189990401127686044">This book was fabulous! I read it as a part of the #TBRTakedown Readathon and as a Buddy Read. It's a little bit on the slow side for sure, but actually it's a very interesting story and the characterisation and development of this was seriously fantastic. It's a slow story which is made up mostly from the introduction of various characters (mostly Traders) and developing our understanding of them and their ways. It's set in a different part of the world from the Farseer Books and it's set on th</span>
  <span id="freeText3189990401127686044" style="display:none">This book was fabulous! I read it as a part of the #TBRTakedown Readathon and as a Buddy Read. It's a little bit on the slow side for sure, but actually it's a very interesting story and the characterisation and development of this was seriously fantastic. It's a slow story which is made up mostly from the introduction of various characters (mostly Traders) and developing our understanding of them and their ways. It's set in a different part of the world from the Farseer Books and it's set on the Cursed Shores (doesn't sound like the nicest area). We join the story when there's a fair amount of outside interference coming into the community of Bingtown, and the Trader families living there are not entirely sure just what to do or how to manage the situation of the new inhabitants trying to come in and change their ways.<br /><br />This is a book which clearly puts the characters at the forefront of the story because despite it being an 880pg book actually only a few very major events stand out. Despite this, there's so much work on defining and understanding the characters that I feel as if I know them all so well now and I can see how they'd react and why they'd react that way in various situations.<br /><br />The world-building of this book is also more unique than that of the Farseer books in that it's largely focused on the sea, and ships at sea, used by the Traders. The old traders of Bingtown are often owners of Liveships which means that they own a ship made of wizard wood for many years and generations and they gradually bond with the ship. Over time this bond develops to the point where the figurehead of the ship will 'quicken' and come to life, filled with the memories and wisdom of all the previous family members it has bonded with.<br />I loved the idea of the Liveships and the way that they become so integral to the town and the trade that they conduct. Not only this, but they are very interesting characters in their own right and the understanding they learn after their quickening can decide how they will react for years to come, being either loyal to the family they are bonded with or turning mad from the grief and savagery introduced to them.<br /><br />We're also introduced not only to the Bingtown Traders in this book but also the Rain Wild Traders who were one of the most mysterious and interesting elements of the book for me. I know that one of Hobb's later series is called the Rain Wild Chronicles and I have to say I am VERY eager to check that one out after what i learned and saw hints of in this book!<br /><br />Pirates and Slavery are big themes within this book and we get to meet one character and crew who have little to do with the Traders other than that they are Pirates who wish to own a Liveship. Everyone knows that a Liveship will only work for the family that it's bonded to and it can easily go mad or savage if it's separated from the family members, but this won't stop the crew who serve under Kennit, a man with high ambitions... <br /><br />The final element I want to point out before diving into the characters is that we also follow some Serpents in this book and we get to see their thoughts as they follow their prey and seek food and wisdom. This section, although initially intriguing, was the only element I feel like I still don't have much interest in, and although we get hints that there's a bigger story ahead involving the Serpents, I didn't find them anywhere near as interesting as the human characters.<br /><br />So, the characters:-<br /><br />- Althea Vestrit - is a young woman who is working on board the Vivacia, her family ship, whilst she waits for it to become quickened. She's a somewhat competent sailor, but she's a little spoiled and she knows that when her father retires or dies she will be the one whom the ship is passed to. She is bold and daring as a character, but she also has some flaws with entitlement and believing she's better than some of the other crew just because she's the captain's daughter. When her father is sick for a long time her story suddenly begins to change pace and things don't always go quite as she may have believed they would, throwing her into some rather tricky situations.<br />I enjoyed Althea's story a lot, although she wasn't my favourite, and seeing her grow as a character and develop more skills and knowledge over the book was very pleasing. She's got a way to go still, but her character was one which grew on me more and more as I got to know her more, and she's a very interesting one to watch.<br /><br />- Paragon - is an old and washed up Liveship whom everyone avoids. He used to be a great Liveship who was proud and happy as any other to serve his family, but something horrible happened and over time he sunk deeper and deeper into madness until he was no longer worth using for fear he would kill the crew he served. He's a sad and forlorn character a lot of the time and he really doesn't have a lot to live for which makes him grumpy and distrustful. <br />I really enjoyed that fact that the ships themselves had pov's in this and that we got to see things from their view as it gave a new perspective on many of the situations. Paragon is a character whose sections instantly gripped me because he was so different to most things I have read before, and his bitter nature was interesting to follow.<br /><br />- Vivacia - is the Vestrit's family Liveship and she's the ship that Althea and her father have worked for all of their lives. She begins the story before she's quickened, and so the events that go on on the ship still affect her, but she has no voice herself for any but those she's bonded with. Once she does become quickened she finds that things are not quite as she'd always imagined they would be and there's actually a lot more hardship and terror ahead for her than she would have ever believed that the Vestrit's would put her through.<br />Vivacia's pov really was great to see, especially as she has the memories of various past Vestrit's within her. She gives us an interesting outlook, one of a newly quickened ship (unlike the Paragon) and she shows us how it is to be born into the life of a Liveship and the toll that this bond can exact upon her.<br /><br />- Brashen - was Captain Vestrit's (Althea's father's) first Mate and he's a well beloved member of the Vivacia. He's a kind and loyal member of the crew and when he sees things turning sour before him he understands that the best thing to do may be to abandon ship and start afresh. Unfortunately, things are not that simple and he's already entangled in the affairs of the Vestrit's, something which will no doubt continue...<br />Brashen is a friend to the Paragon, and he's also a good ship mate. He knows his job and does it thoroughly and well, and he's also a man of common sense (most of the time). I really enjoyed seeing him on his journey, and I liked the way that he dealt with some of the more difficult situations he was put into, using his intelligence. <br /><br />- Kyle Haven - is Althea's brother-in-law and a member of the Vestrit family only by marrying into it. He's a capable sailor and a decent captain, but he's ruthless and only believes in his way. He's always certain that he knows the best way to handle things, and he's unable to see other's points of view even when the evidence of his mistakes are laid bare before him. He's a stubborn and cruel character and whilst he's a little deserving of deference, he's not as deserving of loyalty and love as he first appears.<br />He was certainly the 'bad-guy' of the book for me and I found him rather detestable at times, however it was a very tense moment whenever he intervened and for that his parts kept me intrigued!!<br /><br />- Keffria Vestrit - is the wife of Kyle and sister to Althea. She's a woman who loves and admires her husband so much that she's become accustomed to deferring to him and letting him have his own way both with her and her family. She's a kind and conscientious character who only wishes that she could please everyone, but when everything starts to go wrong and she's in the middle of two strong wills she has to begin to stand tall herself and come into her own.<br />Keffria's character took longer for me to warm to because at first she seemed a little weak and silly, but as the story went on I saw her too grow and become someone I liked a lot and admired for the actions she took.<br /><br />- Wintrow - is the oldest child and son of Kyle and Keffria. He's a true member of the Vestrit blood whether he wants to be or not and he's been in training to become a Priest of Sa for most of his young life. He believe's strongly in Sa's teachings and the ways of following his God, and he's a soft-natured and gentle young man. <br />He's the character that I think I was most easily connected to early on because of his genteel nature and the way that he approached difficult situations and always tried to do the 'right' thing. He may not have always handled things in the most efficient and productive ways, but he's a very loyal and careful character and he stays firm to what he believes in no matter what he's subjected to so I admired him immensely for that.<br /><br />- Ronica Vestrit - is the mother of Althea and Keffria and the Grandmother to Wintrow and Malta. She's a strong-willed character who's handled the affairs of the family for as long as her husband has been sailing the Vivacia and she's very competent at what she does. She's kind and careful and reputation matters greatly to her so she always tries to keep up appearances and do the best thing for her family.<br />I think she was a character whom I enjoyed a lot as she was tested more because it brought out her more soft and tender side and showed how vulnerable even the head of the family can be. She's always trying to do the thing she sees best for them all and sometimes she gets things wrong or makes mistakes, but I liked her ability to try new approaches when necessary and acknowledge her mistakes. <br /><br />- Malta - is the daughter and second child of Kyle and Keffria and she's a very spoilt young girl. She wants things to be her way and none other and she follows firmly in her father's way of managing things. She's silly and foolish and makes many grave mistakes over the course of the book but she's also young and naive and doesn't fully understand the results of her actions.<br />I found her to be one of the most irritating and yet interesting characters and storylines because she made mistake after mistake and refused to bend or apologise even when she was caught out. Her will is as strong as her father's and grandmother's and she tested her family sorely many times.<br /><br />- Captain Kennit - is the pirate Captain of a ship who desires his own Liveship more than anything. After hearing a prophecy about himself at the start of the book he acts upon what he believes as his right and aims to capture and acquire a Liveship for himself. He's a dark and very cruel man with a skill for manipulation and pain. He desires nothing more than reaching his goals and if he has to be a bloodthirsty Pirate to do so he will, but he's equally a fantastic character whose inner thoughts were great to read.<br />I enjoyed seeing the development of him as a character and learning more about how he worked and planned out his moves. He's crafty, thinks highly of himself, and he uses all of this to his advantage to achieve his aims. Certainly another one to watch! <br /><br />So as you can see there's a range and collection of characters who are all very distinct and yet are connected together in various ways. Hobb's development in this book of these characters leads me to believe that the plot of the next two should be a little faster paced and we will begin to learn more of the other elements of the world, but I a, sure there will still be more development and tests ahead for our characters.<br /><br />Hobb certainly didn't shy away from a more dark and gritty reality in this book. She approaches topic such as slavery and gives great insights into how it would have been to be a slave or slaver and she integrates this into the story in a seamless way, making it a key part of the world and plot. She also manages to involve politics and mystery into the book, making it not only thought-provoking but also tense.<br /><br />On the whole, my favourite Hobb book by far and I hope to start the next one in this series sometime later this month to see what will happen next. A wonderful story and a slow but fantastic book, 5*s - highly recommended!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3189990401127686044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_134932524" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134932524" />
    <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon"><img alt="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572581488p2/1209800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/134932524?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon">colleen the convivial curmudgeon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553103243" href="/book/show/1833120.Ship_of_Magic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=group-read">group-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer134932524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15700341787387551484">12/21/10<br/><br/>I'm about 75% through with this book, and I'm finding it frustrating. <br/><br/>As others have said, it's very much a character-based book, and I can dig character-based books if I like the characters, but I'm having a hard time really latching onto anyone that I don't want to smack upside the head. <br/><br/>Actually, no, I do like some characters (Brashen and Paragon, for instance) - but the ones I do like we don't seem to spend enough time with, while we spend far too much time with the likes of Kyle and</span>
  <span id="freeText15700341787387551484" style="display:none">12/21/10<br /><br />I'm about 75% through with this book, and I'm finding it frustrating. <br /><br />As others have said, it's very much a character-based book, and I can dig character-based books if I like the characters, but I'm having a hard time really latching onto anyone that I don't want to smack upside the head. <br /><br />Actually, no, I do like some characters (Brashen and Paragon, for instance) - but the ones I do like we don't seem to spend enough time with, while we spend far too much time with the likes of Kyle and Malta. <br /><br />And I have a love-hate relationship with the shifting perspectives. When I'm slogging through a particularlty annoying or slow perspective, I'm grateful for its end, but there are other times when things are finally get interesting, only for the action to then cut-away from what's going on, and I have to wait 150 more pages to get back to what I was interested in. (And then, when we do get back to it, often time has passed, and so we're not taken back to the moment that had captured me anyway.) <br /><br />So far, I've been reading this book for 9 days. That's a long time for me to take on one book. Part of the problem is that I'm just not really motivated to pick it up. I'm not attached enough to the characters to long for the time when I can pick the book back up, and, sometimes, I even find myself putting it off during my daily allotted reading time. <br /><br />But I don't hate it. Thus far, I would probably rate it 2 stars. And I guess that's what's so frustrating, because I think I could like it more, like it could almost be a book I loved, but it's just not. *shrugs*<br /><br />***<br /><br />12/22/10<br /><br />So I finally finished. I was promised some actual character development by the end, and it did happen, of a sort. Also, some stuff came together and there was actually some action. Yay! I wish that the events hadn't been quite so predictable, but at least the last 100 pages or so moved at a better pace.<br /><br />I know do feel the need to continue, when, before, it was more of a "I suppose I must", but a lot of this is because nothing gets resolved in this book. It's definitely not a stand alone.<br /><br />Anyway, even though I feel slightly more favorable to the book than I did above, I still feel like it could've been chopped down, a lot of the character set-up was repetitious and tedious, and I can easily see how some scenes could've been combined. <br /><br />I'm still not sure I like any of the more major players, though.<br /><br />1.5</span>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8352877215803000690">It started slow for me until I realized that nothing much was going to happen until the extended family all had their say. <br/><br/>That being said, the plot started weaving and the world started blooming. So many bad things started happening to everyone so slowly that I wondered if I, too, was slowly being boiled alive.<br/><br/>That's the effect this novel had on me. It's very long, and its very detailed. If you like immersive fantasy and especially nautical fantasy, then you'll love this.<br/><br/>Edit 7/5/16<br/><br/>Looking back</span>
  <span id="freeText8352877215803000690" style="display:none">It started slow for me until I realized that nothing much was going to happen until the extended family all had their say. <br /><br />That being said, the plot started weaving and the world started blooming. So many bad things started happening to everyone so slowly that I wondered if I, too, was slowly being boiled alive.<br /><br />That's the effect this novel had on me. It's very long, and its very detailed. If you like immersive fantasy and especially nautical fantasy, then you'll love this.<br /><br />Edit 7/5/16<br /><br />Looking back after years and having read the full trilogy plus a third trilogy after this one, I'm a bit more forgiving of the novel. The final interesting events, the redemption and restoration of the mad ship, the tragedy of the main family, and all the proto-dragons, the leviathans, and the wilds, makes me think much more fondly on the whole storyline. :)</span>

<div id="review_1628932946" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1628932946" />
    <a title="Amy | littledevonnook" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10559838-amy-littledevonnook"><img alt="Amy | littledevonnook" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596620580p2/10559838.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1628932946?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy | littledevonnook" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy | littledevonnook" href="/user/show/10559838-amy-littledevonnook">Amy | littledevonnook</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1628932946" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6377388138332949991">I think this could be the one of the best fantasy books I've read so far this year - I can't wait to see what the rest of this trilogy holds!<br/><br/>This series is set in the same world at the Farseer Trilogy and so far I am enjoying it a lot more! Unlike the Farseer books The Liveship Traders follows a larger group of characters - from land to sea we are given a whole host of exciting people to share adventures with.<br/><br/>One of our main characters is a young lady named Althea. She lives aboard her families </span>
  <span id="freeText6377388138332949991" style="display:none">I think this could be the one of the best fantasy books I've read so far this year - I can't wait to see what the rest of this trilogy holds!<br /><br />This series is set in the same world at the Farseer Trilogy and so far I am enjoying it a lot more! Unlike the Farseer books The Liveship Traders follows a larger group of characters - from land to sea we are given a whole host of exciting people to share adventures with.<br /><br />One of our main characters is a young lady named Althea. She lives aboard her families liveship named Vivacia. Once a certain number of generations have died aboard the decks of a liveship the figurehead comes to life - at the very beginning of the book Althea's father dies and Vivacia is freed from her static life. Althea's dream of captaining the ship are quickly taken away by her sister's gruesome husband - it is then Althea's mission to regain the captaincy of her families ship!<br /><br />There are so many other things happening in this novel that I wouldn't be able to explain it all here. I would simply say that if you enjoy fantasy and you are looking for a exciting ride I would highly recommend you pick this one up! Robin Hobb is a wonderful writer and I can't wait to see what happens next!</span>

<div id="review_1346703640" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1346703640" />
    <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen"><img alt="Helene Jeppesen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528006866p2/21992464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1346703640?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helene Jeppesen" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen">Helene Jeppesen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007459728" href="/book/show/13400626-ship-of-magic">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1346703640" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13288703793800591695">If you're looking for a great and original fantasy story with a big set of characters and an amazing world building, then this is it. Robin Hobb is a master at creating suspenseful stories with vivid and interesting characters that you feel a connection to. In this book, you even feel a connection to the ships!<br/>What I especially like about Robin Hobb's books is that she makes fantasy accessible to me. I'm not the biggest reader of fantasy, but when I do read it I want to be enchanted with the wor</span>
  <span id="freeText13288703793800591695" style="display:none">If you're looking for a great and original fantasy story with a big set of characters and an amazing world building, then this is it. Robin Hobb is a master at creating suspenseful stories with vivid and interesting characters that you feel a connection to. In this book, you even feel a connection to the ships!<br />What I especially like about Robin Hobb's books is that she makes fantasy accessible to me. I'm not the biggest reader of fantasy, but when I do read it I want to be enchanted with the world. I always am when I read Robin Hobb's books. <br />Now, while I really liked this story and definitely recommend it, I didn't rate it 5 stars. That's because even though I did find the plot very interesting, intricate and just about complex enough, I also felt like some elements of the story became too silly in my eyes. I sometimes questioned what was happening - not because it didn't fit it with the story and the world, but because I didn't see the deeper meaning of it. Sometimes it felt like Robin Hobb used a lot of fantastical elements that you can expect from a story like this, and I guess I just missed the element of surprise. <br />Furthermore, while I did love all the characters (their weaknesses as well), they were written as caricatures, and almost all characters lacked nuance in their behaviour. Either they were the good guys, or the evil ones, and they didn't differ from that place. I would've loved for Robin Hobb to bring it up a notch and give the reader the possibility to actually connect with the bad guys as well, and to give the good guys some weaknesses. In my eyes, that would have made the story even better.<br />Nevertheless, this is absolutely great fantasy which takes you on quite a journey, and I'm very interested to see what will happen to these characters in the upcoming books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13288703793800591695" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Sade" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16037420-sade"><img alt="Sade" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605390492p2/16037420.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sade" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sade" href="/user/show/16037420-sade">Sade</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2046988646" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14134819588753157977"> <blockquote><br/>It will never cease to amaze me how writers can take words, spin it and make you care about characters that exist only in books, make you care about the words these characters utter, how because of words on a page, you're rooting for a character to be better, stronger, braver. It's awe inspiring and just amazing.<br/><br/>Robin Hobb is one of those writers that weaves magic with her words. and it's curious, it's not like her books at least the few i've read have an insane amount of gore or are especially</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText14134819588753157977" style="display:none"> <blockquote><br />It will never cease to amaze me how writers can take words, spin it and make you care about characters that exist only in books, make you care about the words these characters utter, how because of words on a page, you're rooting for a character to be better, stronger, braver. It's awe inspiring and just amazing.<br /><br />Robin Hobb is one of those writers that weaves magic with her words. and it's curious, it's not like her books at least the few i've read have an insane amount of gore or are especially grim. but somehow she's captures the essence of a character so thoroughly. <i>You can feel the selfishness of Malta, the apathy that dictated Keffria life, the strength that was Ronica Vestrit, the confusion peppered with shadows of strength, wisdom and the occasional dose of stupidity that was Wintrow, the stinking mess of insecurity that was Kyle Haven, the fire cracker that was Althea Vestrit and the ships, gosh the ships.....</i><br /><br />I did feel sometimes descriptions ran a tad too long but having read the Farseer trilogy, i've come to recognise that as signature Hobb story telling..<br /><b>All in all a truly delightful book that does not disappoint.</b><br /></blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="14134819588753157977" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2473782138" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2473782138" />
    <a title="Anthony" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4009947-anthony"><img alt="Anthony" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534088626p2/4009947.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2473782138?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anthony" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anthony" href="/user/show/4009947-anthony">Anthony</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780553900255" href="/book/show/6991075-ship-of-magic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=sf-group-2018">sf-group-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=7-kingdoms-challenge">7-kingdoms-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=time-traveler-challenge">time-traveler-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2473782138" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9912598307814839939">Another master class given by Robin Hobb in characterization, pacing, plotting, stakes, and emotional truth, all delivered in her clear, brutal, graceful prose. I marvel at the skill with which she pivoted from a first-person narrative in The Farseer Trilogy to that of this novel, which is told with multiple viewpoints, all convincingly and humanely brought to life, even the most despicable or complex of them. It had been a while since I was this satisfied with a book, and I am grateful. </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2473782138">

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2303648622" />
    <a title="Scott  Hitchcock" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50894754-scott-hitchcock"><img alt="Scott  Hitchcock" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459187975p2/50894754.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2303648622?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott  Hitchcock" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott  Hitchcock" href="/user/show/50894754-scott-hitchcock">Scott  Hitchcock</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781400184378" href="/book/show/9848101-ship-of-magic">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Scott  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller">Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50894754-scott-hitchcock?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2303648622" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17951412058455438208">A big thanks to Niki and Bill who convinced me this was worth reading in spite of the Farseer trilogy which while well written drove me crazy but Fitz might be the worst protagonist, EVER! <br/><br/>4.5*'s<br/><br/>This book had all the elements I love in fantasy. Smart and real characters who weren't black and white. They all had motivations which led them to both good and bad decisions. <br/><br/>Different types of magic and magical creatures and you weren't just told about them, you were made to feel them. What they were </span>
  <span id="freeText17951412058455438208" style="display:none">A big thanks to Niki and Bill who convinced me this was worth reading in spite of the Farseer trilogy which while well written drove me crazy but Fitz might be the worst protagonist, EVER! <br /><br />4.5*'s<br /><br />This book had all the elements I love in fantasy. Smart and real characters who weren't black and white. They all had motivations which led them to both good and bad decisions. <br /><br />Different types of magic and magical creatures and you weren't just told about them, you were made to feel them. What they were about. What they felt. How they interacted with the world and the characters. <br /><br />There was real trauma and hardship, tough decisions to be made. Strife between conflicting characters and their points of view. A lot was left unanswered for us which I love. Don't show me everything at once, play the long game. The customs of the different people interwoven into their lives. <br /><br />I especially love the two ships. To me they are so unique. Looking forward to seeing how their stories play out and for the rest of the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17951412058455438208" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2343679483" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2343679483" />
    <a title="Ferdy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy"><img alt="Ferdy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487898103p2/4596358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2343679483?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ferdy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ferdy" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy">Ferdy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12479384-ship-of-magic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=multiple-pov">multiple-pov</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2343679483" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10761157467052912696">2.5 stars <br/><br/>Not as good as the Fitz books, mainly because bar a few characters there was hardly anyone to properly root for or to even feel mildly connected to. There were way too many characters and POVs, and it felt like ages before things really kicked off, it was a really slow start.<br/><br/>Pretty much everyone was unlikeable, even the characters that were meant to be likeable were mostly unlikeable. And they were quite a few boring characters as well, mainly Wintrow, Althea and Brashen.. they did get</span>
  <span id="freeText10761157467052912696" style="display:none">2.5 stars <br /><br />Not as good as the Fitz books, mainly because bar a few characters there was hardly anyone to properly root for or to even feel mildly connected to. There were way too many characters and POVs, and it felt like ages before things really kicked off, it was a really slow start.<br /><br />Pretty much everyone was unlikeable, even the characters that were meant to be likeable were mostly unlikeable. And they were quite a few boring characters as well, mainly Wintrow, Althea and Brashen.. they did get somewhat interesting by the end but it took too long to get there.<br /><br />Loved Kennit and the pirates, they were fantastic. The whole idea of liveships was brilliant too. Best of all though was Paragon, he was the most interesting and easy to root for, loved everything about him.<br /><br />I was really expecting the ship Vivacia to be an amazing character, but she was rubbish, as soon as she quickened all she did was whine and bitch, she had no endearing qualities about her. She had no loyalty to anyone, she flip flopped between Althea, Wintrow and Kennit so easily, and even though she was a ship she somehow managed to be a vapid, shallow, attention seeking twit who latched on to whoever paid her the slightest bit of attention.<br /><br />Wintrow was too thick for words, his every decision was idiotic. Worst of all was his sanctimonious, holier than thou religious talk, he really did think he was better than everyone else, despite being useless and dull. And it was hilarious how he judged anyone who was stuck in a difficult decision for not doing this or that or for not thinking one way instead of another, he always had some superior answer to everything, but as soon as he was in an impossible situation himself he couldn't muster up any solution to get himself out if it. No, he just did daft thing after daft thing and dug himself deeper into trouble.<br /><br />Althea's family were dicks, talk about screwing her over. Althea spent half her life training to take over her family's liveship, that was all she cared about, she had her dad's support and knowledge, she understood the work and would have made a decent captain and ultimately helped the family out of debt. But her awful mum engineered things so Althea wouldn't inherit the ship all so she could control her and marry her off to some rich guy who could help the family. Then she stupidly gave the inheritance to Keffria instead, the doormat eldest daughter who was completely controlled by her slimy husband.. WTF was she thinking? It was disturbing how cool she was with betraying Althea all so she could manipulate and control her into being the dutiful daughter. She was only sorry after she realised her son-in-law wasn't going to do things her way and was taking over as head of the family and could now control her as well as the household, then it dawned on her what a big mistake she made and what a horrible position she was in now. The hypocrite got what she deserved, she fucked over Althea well and truly, then got all regretful and upset when all her careful plans to get Althea under her thumb backfired and she ended up being the one at the mercy of her slimy so -in-law. She had no right to act all outraged when the tables turned on her and it was impossible to feel any sympathy for her situation after she treated her daughter the way she didn't want to be treated herself.<br /><br />Brashen was meant to be the good guy who was down on his luck and had it hard but everything about him pissed me off. I mean, the guy bitched about Althea's attitude and offered her little sympathy or support on the day her dad died, her inheritance was stolen from her and her family betrayed her. There was no kindness, only judgement at how Althea was acting and behaving. Seriously, the guy had no compassion whatsoever. Everything was about him and his pain, I just didn't care about him at all.<br /><br />Last of all, the serpents were terrible, I felt like dozing off in their parts, they had relatively short POVs but they felt so long and drawn out. They didn't fit in with the rest of the story/characters, and I didn't see the point of their particular arc.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10761157467052912696" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/143947306?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat" href="/user/show/4878104-kat">Kat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=intriguing-fucked-up-men">intriguing-fucked-up-men</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=wow-re-read-material">wow-re-read-material</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=terrific-covers">terrific-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=all-nighters">all-nighters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=rad-badass-heroines-or-heroes">rad-badass-heroines-or-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=pirates">pirates</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4878104-kat?shelf=binnengehaald">binnengehaald</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143947306" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13992221526790505385">March 2014: Buddy read with Kat, Damian and Em. Ooooooh, Kennit! If I had to choose between you and Toreth, I'd have to chop myself in half.:')<br/> <br/>Yep, I still stand by my hysterically enthusiastic review from a few years ago *happy sigh*.<br/><br/>__________________________<br/><br/><b>2011 fan squealing below :p:</b> <br/>Woot woot..Wow, this trilogy is incredible. <br/>I mean, I've re-read these bible-sized books three to four times. And I keep discovering new bits and pieces, new clues in this extremely rich, yes epic, (now that I</span>
  <span id="freeText13992221526790505385" style="display:none">March 2014: Buddy read with Kat, Damian and Em. Ooooooh, Kennit! If I had to choose between you and Toreth, I'd have to chop myself in half.:')<br /> <br />Yep, I still stand by my hysterically enthusiastic review from a few years ago *happy sigh*.<br /><br />__________________________<br /><br /><b>2011 fan squealing below :p:</b> <br />Woot woot..Wow, this trilogy is incredible. <br />I mean, I've re-read these bible-sized books three to four times. And I keep discovering new bits and pieces, new clues in this extremely rich, yes epic, (now that I'm on a superlatives-roll: MINDBLOWING) story. <br /><br />Sure, Hobb's first trilogy was such an intense reading experience. I was quite young when I discovered the first <i>Farseer</i> book and I felt like I could almost crawl into Fitz's skin and live his life with him. And Night Eyes' life! I forgot to study. I started missing my train station. I had to wait for half an hour on the opposite platform, in the cold, not minding. I skipped meals so I could keep reading (which is a highly unusual thing for me to do) etc etc..you get the picture?<br /><br />Now <i>The Liveship Traders</i> trilogy is a little different, mostly because Hobb no longer focuses on one character, but introduces a whole bunch of three-dimensional ones. I know how some reviewers keep missing Fitz, but I personally found these books even more compelling.<br /><br />If you like straight forward fantasy books with a main character going on a quest, Hobb's books are probably not for you. As I mentioned, she introduces many, brilliant characters that are all starring in a spectacular fantasy story including evil, yet charming pirates, tough girls' running from home, a sinister island, sea snakes and a long forgotten tribe, that in reality is very much alive in the blood of some people in Bingtown...<br />I particularly liked that, although Hobb definitely makes sure to add plenty of tragedy, drama and torture to <i>The Liveship Traders</i> as well, she didn't go overboard this time. If Fitz had been a real person, the poor fellow would probably have been dead and buried six times already after everything Hobb cooked up for him. <br /><br />Fans of Fitz will enjoy the references and clues to him, that Hobb included in this trilogy. Although reading her first trilogy before this one is not necessary, I would recommend doing so because, let's face it; you'll probably want to do so anyway afterwards. <br /><br />I just wish Hobb would write a trilogy starring pirate Kennit...hey, a girl can dream!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13992221526790505385" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2851823042?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aaron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aaron" href="/user/show/79040572-aaron">Aaron</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2851823042" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4930752850476230056">***4.5 stars<br/><br/>This was a buddy read with a group from Epic fantasy books. <br/><br/>I went into this book expecting to enjoy it because I enjoyed the Farseer trilogy. Hobb’s writing is great. In this book even when events weren’t moving along quickly the writing was so good that it kept me wanting to read. There were parts when I was ready for the plot to move along. Looking back I realize that Hobb was using that time to develop the characters so it doesn’t bother me anymore. The plot was interesting with </span>
  <span id="freeText4930752850476230056" style="display:none">***4.5 stars<br /><br />This was a buddy read with a group from Epic fantasy books. <br /><br />I went into this book expecting to enjoy it because I enjoyed the Farseer trilogy. Hobb’s writing is great. In this book even when events weren’t moving along quickly the writing was so good that it kept me wanting to read. There were parts when I was ready for the plot to move along. Looking back I realize that Hobb was using that time to develop the characters so it doesn’t bother me anymore. The plot was interesting with many different players and events throughout the book. The ending of the book wrapped somethings up but left enough open to keep me wondering what would happen next and wanting to continue the series. A great first book to the second series in Hobb’s world, but I have to say it was made even better by the discussion that went along from my group!</span>

<div id="review_754388090" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/754388090" />
    <a title="Wanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda"><img alt="Wanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528903039p2/9246169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/754388090?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wanda" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda">Wanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/24854871-ship-of-magic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=z-1990s">z-1990s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=female-authors">female-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=public-library">public-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=reading-project">reading-project</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=2020-reading-list">2020-reading-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=pirates-arrr">pirates-arrr</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer754388090" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15802262677476648615">I've been looking forward to this book and returning to the world of the <i>Farseer Trilogy</i>. Imagine my surprise at how completely different this story was. Oh, there was a reference to the appearance of dragons at some point in the recent past, but there was otherwise no overlap.<br/><br/>The Liveships are a wonderful idea—with their frames made from wizardwood, they eventually gain some level of sentience & personality. Once quickened, the ship is able to assist its captain and crew. As the book progresses</span>
  <span id="freeText15802262677476648615" style="display:none">I've been looking forward to this book and returning to the world of the <i>Farseer Trilogy</i>. Imagine my surprise at how completely different this story was. Oh, there was a reference to the appearance of dragons at some point in the recent past, but there was otherwise no overlap.<br /><br />The Liveships are a wonderful idea—with their frames made from wizardwood, they eventually gain some level of sentience &amp; personality. Once quickened, the ship is able to assist its captain and crew. As the book progresses, we learn more about the mystical bond between a Liveship and the family that commissioned it. Mystery seems to be a detriment to the current situation, as the uninitiated don't appreciate the needs of these amazing beings for a living link to their owners. And it is made clear that there is a definite link between the production of Liveships owned by the Bingtown traders and the Rain Wild River people, with their disfigured faces and their great wealth. There is a mysterious contract which both sides must adhere to, blood or gold. <br /><br />You can read the book just as a tale of family dynamics, a family business having difficulty with the process of succession, or you can interpret things more deeply. What to make of Kyle Haven, who desperately wants to be a respected patriarch but doesn't realize that control doesn't mean lording it over everyone else in the family. He criticizes Althea as spoiled and then turns around and makes his own daughter, Malta, infinitely worse. A man who is willing to transport slaves and expects slavish devotion from his family &amp; crew. I can't help disliking the man, but also find myself pitying him. <br /><br />Also interesting are the sea monsters that plague those who sail the oceans. They seem to be merely predators, but we are privy to some of their thoughts in short vignettes and we watch their behaviour shifting during the course of the book. Their ultimate fate (and their relationship with the ship Vivacia) is merely hinted at in this volume.<br /><br />I will definitely be reading on when I get a chance. What happens to Althea? Does the mad ship Paragon make nice with anyone? Do Althea and Brashen find their way back together? (That's a foregone conclusion, I would guess). What does Malta make of her Rain Wild River suitor? Will Wintrow ever recover some kind of relationship with his family? Or will a pirate conquer the Vivacia's heart?<br /><br />Hobb leaves us with so many interesting questions. She is very skillful at manipulating my emotions and leading me on to the next book.<br /><br /><b>Book number 377 of my Science Fiction &amp; Fantasy Reading Project.</b><br /><br />Cross posted at my blog:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://wanda-thenextfifty.blogspot.com/2020/08/ship-of-magic-robin-hobb.html">https://wanda-thenextfifty.blogspot.c...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15802262677476648615" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1446513677" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1446513677" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8575414-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441431450p2/8575414.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1446513677?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/8575414-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8575414-emma?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8575414-emma?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1446513677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10871527346512114505">Even better on a reread! This is the trilogy that some Hobb fans put off reading. I did myself for a long time. But it really does have a magic all of its own and of course this time round, understanding how it all fits together in the Realm of the Elderlings, means the foreshadowing is easier to spot. Such a cast of characters! And character depth and development for them all- through this book and the trilogy</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_507477029" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/507477029" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2431873-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1477433724p2/2431873.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/507477029?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/2431873-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553575637" href="/book/show/618211.Ship_of_Magic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2431873-emily?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2431873-emily?shelf=ships-and-seafaring">ships-and-seafaring</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer507477029" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3496681055878418060">I have very mixed feelings about this book. At this point, I'm invested - to the tune of 800 pages - and I liked the world and the general direction the series seems to be going in. Even with 800 pages, though, it felt like Hobb ran out of room to truly develop the world, and because this is a trilogy the characters end up at (what I hope is) the nadir of their fortunes at the end of the book. All of it feels a little incomplete. I'll end up reading on, but before I do:<br/><br/><b>Things I Really Liked</b><br/>- The</span>
  <span id="freeText3496681055878418060" style="display:none">I have very mixed feelings about this book. At this point, I'm invested - to the tune of 800 pages - and I liked the world and the general direction the series seems to be going in. Even with 800 pages, though, it felt like Hobb ran out of room to truly develop the world, and because this is a trilogy the characters end up at (what I hope is) the nadir of their fortunes at the end of the book. All of it feels a little incomplete. I'll end up reading on, but before I do:<br /><br /><b>Things I Really Liked</b><br />- The history between the Rain Wild Traders and the Bingtown Traders, while not explored that deeply in this book, is fascinating and something I haven't seen much of in other fantasy books. I am really excited to get into the reasons why the Vestrits have stopped trading up the river. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I hope Malta gets married off so there can be scenes there. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />- I am a sucker for Girls Sailing, Girls Sailing as Boys, Forbidden Love at Sea, and any number of other fantasy seafaring tropes. A++ would like more of all of this please.<br /><br />- Kennit's obvious sociopathy tickles me. He's interesting to read because his perspective is so skewed. I did spend the first 300 pages reading "Kermit," though.<br /><br /><br /><b>Things I Didn't Like As Much As I Thought I Would</b><br />- The characters are particularly tough in this book. Around page 200, all of them are terrible, but they begin to even out as you spend more time with them. The characters develop, sure, but they <i>have</i> to for the reader to stand them. I thought I was going to like Althea Vestrit a lot more than I did. I never thought I would like Malta, but I would like to point out the distinct Alison DiLaurentis vibe I'm getting from her. (Anyone? Is this the right part of Goodreads for that comparison?)<br /><br />- I'm not 100% sold on the liveships. I like the concept (maybe?). I don't know. I need some more time to sort out my feelings. I have a hard time both visualizing and understanding how Vivacia is interacting with the humans and how her figurehead is positioned on the ship.<br /><br /><br /><b>Things I Really Didn't Like</b><br />- This book is all about the characters' fortunes in free-fall, which makes the ending sort of depressing. The reversal of Wintrow's fortunes was particularly hard to read. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Something about the slave tattoo really gets me. There's no coming back from that. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />- The multiple perspectives are edited very poorly. Nowhere is this more apparent than in the first long scene in the book with Kennit on the Others' island. During that scene, Hobb cuts to Wintrow in the monastery before coming back (??). It completely kills the suspense, kills interest in Wintrow, and feels very uneven. In fact, she kept cutting from all of the interesting bits, and I found myself skimming forward to find out what was going to happen, which I very rarely do. It's not like she inserts cliffhangers - it's like someone took a pair of scissors to the narratives and just arranged them at random.<br /><br />- Kyle Haven feels like a cardboard cutout of a villain. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Everyone's 180 turn on how they feel about Kyle - particularly Ronica Vestrit! - is just too much. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It's so obvious that he's awful that it's boring and unrealistic.<br /><br />- The map included in the front is terrible! None of the locations that I care about are represented. Where is the Rain Wild River?? Where is Chalced? Why does the map of Bingtown have depth indicators for Trader Bay, but no map of Bingtown itself? This drives me batty. I love when fantasy books include a map in the front (bonus points for a nice family tree in semi-ornate font), but it would have been better to have no map at all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3496681055878418060" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('diLWBhDaCD6vwha44cLz2yoSIk9woj5xDwXrkpgHufPzVQdsqLXQtoqNvtswDu0leDJegozSppblmSq1BiTuAA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb">About Robin Hobb</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1397885202p3/25307.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb">Robin Hobb
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
80,262
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4613436339835314963">** I am shocked to find that some people think a 2 star 'I liked it' rating is a bad rating. What? I liked it. I LIKED it! That means I read the whole thing, to the last page, in spite of my life raining comets on me. It's a good book that survives the reading process with me. If a book is so-so, it ends up under the bed somewhere, or maybe under a stinky judo bag in the back of the van. So a 2 st</span>
  <span id="freeText4613436339835314963" style="display:none">** I am shocked to find that some people think a 2 star 'I liked it' rating is a bad rating. What? I liked it. I LIKED it! That means I read the whole thing, to the last page, in spite of my life raining comets on me. It's a good book that survives the reading process with me. If a book is so-so, it ends up under the bed somewhere, or maybe under a stinky judo bag in the back of the van. So a 2 star from me means,yes, I liked the book, and I'd loan it to a friend and it went everywhere in my jacket pocket or purse until I finished it. A 3 star means that I've ignored friends to finish it and my sink is full of dirty dishes. A 4 star means I'm probably in trouble with my editor for missing a deadline because I was reading this book. But I want you to know . . . I don't finish books I don't like. There's too many good ones out there waiting to be found.<br /><br /><br />Robin Hobb is the author of three well-received fantasy trilogies: The Farseer Trilogy (Assassin’s Apprentice, Royal Assassin, and Assassin’s Quest), The Liveship Traders Trilogy (Ship of Magic, Mad Ship and Ship of Destiny) and the Tawny Man Trilogy (Fool’s Errand, Golden Fool, and Fool’s Fate) Her current work in progress is entitled Shaman’s Crossing. Robin Hobb lives and works in Tacoma, Washington, and has been a professional writer for over 30 years.<br /><br />In addition to writing, her interests include gardening, mushrooming, and beachcombing. She and her husband Fred have three grown children and one teenager, and three grand-children.<br /><br />She also writes as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/53255.Megan_Lindholm" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Lindholm</a>, and works under that name have been finalists for the Hugo award, the Nebula Award, and the Endeavor award. She has twice won an Isaac Asimov’s Science Fiction Readers’ Award.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4613436339835314963" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
